Allah's names like al-Khaliq are based on His eternal attributes, not on the occurrence of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says Allah has 'Lordship without a lorded' and 'Creator-ness without a created.' This means He is perfect in Himself regardless of creation. Does your relationship with Allah depend on the blessings He gives you, or do you worship Him for who He is even when you feel alone or destitute?

Divine Knowledge as an Essential Attribute and His Command and Prohibition
Commentary on Allah's essential knowledge and His command and prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge is an eternal essential attribute encompassing all things, and that He commands obedience and forbids disobedience with corresponding rewards and punishments.

Core Idea
Allah’s knowledge covers absolutely everything, and His command and prohibition are rooted in His justice.

This passage from the Sharh Tahawiyyah teaches us two foundational aspects of Allah's attributes and His relationship with creation. First, it establishes that knowledge is an essential, eternal attribute of Allah that encompasses every conceivable thing—from the smallest atom to universals and impossibles. Then it reminds us that Allah's command to obey and prohibition of sin come with clear promises of mercy and threats of punishment. This brief but profound text grounds our understanding of both Allah's omniscience and His moral law.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage combines two distinct topics in one paragraph.
2

Identify how the passage defines knowledge as an essential, eternal attribute. Then notice the list of categories that Allah's knowledge encompasses.
The phrase 'من الجزئيات والكليات والموجودات والمعدومات والممكنات والمستحيلات' is crucial.
3
Understand the command and prohibition
Read the second part about command and prohibition. What is promised for obedience? What is threatened for disobedience?
This shows the connection between knowledge and ethical guidance.

The commentator then mentions that Allah commanded obedience and forbade disobedience, attaching promise of mercy and threat of punishment respectively.

God's Knowledge: An Eternal and All-Encompassing Attribute
Definition and enumeration of God's knowledge as an essential, eternal, and comprehensive attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's knowledge is an essential, eternal attribute that encompasses all things, including particulars, universals, existents, non-existents, possibles, and impossibles.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is unlimited and covers everything, from atoms to abstractions.

This passage from the Sharh Tahawiyyah establishes one of the core divine attributes: knowledge (al-ʿilm). The author, Imam Maydani, explains that God's knowledge is not acquired or limited; it is eternal and intrinsic, and it covers absolutely everything — not only what exists, but also what does not exist, what is possible, and even what is impossible. This lesson unpacks that profound statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original text to get its rhythm and key terms. Note that the passage is concise yet comprehensive.
The Arabic uses technical terms like 'al-ʿilm' and 'al-ṣifa al-dhātiyya'.
2
Identify the two key characteristics
Notice that knowledge is described as essential (dhātī) and eternal (azalī). These are foundational for understanding God's attributes.
Essential means it is intrinsic to God's essence; eternal means it has no beginning.
3
List the categories of known things
The passage enumerates six pairs: particulars & universals, existents & non-existents, possibles & impossibles. Reflect on why all these are included.
Including non-existents and impossibles shows that nothing escapes God's knowledge.
4
Connect to the broader creed
Reflect on how this attribute relates to other attributes like power and will, and why comprehensiveness of knowledge is essential for tawḥīd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعلم صفة من صفاته الذاتية، وهي صفة أزلية تنكشف بها المعلومات عند تعلقها بها؛ فالله تعالى عالم بجميع الموجودات لا يعزب عن علمه مثقال ذرة في الأرض والسموات، بل أحاط بكل شيء علمًا من الجزئيات والكليات والموجودات والمعدومات والممكنات والمستحيلات؛ فهو بكل شيء عليم من الذوات والصفات.
And knowledge is one of His essential attributes, and it is an eternal attribute by which known things are disclosed when they are related to it; so Allah, exalted, is knowledgeable of all existent things, not absent from His knowledge the weight of an atom in the heavens or the earth, rather He encompasses everything in knowledge, from particulars, universals, existents, non-existents, possibles, and impossibles; so He is of everything Knowing, of essences and attributes.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of knowledge. It begins by stating that knowledge is one of God's essential (ذاتية) attributes, meaning it is intrinsic to His essence, not acquired. It is described as eternal (أزلية), having no beginning. Through this attribute, known things (المعلومات) become manifest when they are related to it. The passage then emphasises the comprehensiveness of God's knowledge: He knows all existent things, nothing escapes Him, not even an atom's weight. It enumerates the categories of things God knows: particulars (الجزئيات) and universals (الكليات), existents (الموجودات) and non-existents (المعدومات), possibles (الممكنات) and impossibles (المستحيلات). It concludes that God knows all essences (الذوات) and attributes (الصفات). This affirms the orthodox Sunni doctrine that God's knowledge is all-encompassing and eternal, rejecting any limitation.

The Divine Decree: Guidance and Misguidance as Favor and Justice
Creedal statement on divine guidance and misguidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's guidance, protection, and well-being are acts of favor, while misguidance, abandonment, and affliction are acts of justice, and that no one can oppose His decree.

Core Idea
God's actions are either favor or justice; His decree is irresistible.

The creed of Ahl al-Sunnah affirms that all divine acts are purposeful—guidance and protection are pure favor, while misguidance and affliction are just. This passage lays the foundation for understanding divine providence without attributing evil to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb the rhythm of the creed. Then read the translation.
Notice the parallel structure between favor and justice.
2
Identify the two categories
Identify which acts are labeled as favor (فضل) and which as justice (عدل). Reflect on why misguidance can be just.
Justice does not imply evil; it means God acts according to His wisdom.
3
Reflect on God's transcendence
The passage states God is exalted above opposites and rivals. Consider how this reinforces His absolute sovereignty.
4
Affirm the creed
End by internalizing the statement 'We believe in all of that' and recognize that everything is from Him.

(ويعاني) أي يدفع عن من يشاء) عافيته، وهي دفاع الله تعالى عن العبد. مختار (1) (فضلا) منه ومنة، ويضل من يشاء) إضلاله، وهو ضد الرشاد، (ويخذل) - بضم -الذال يترك نصرته وعونه ( ويبتلي) بالشر من يشاء خذلانه وابتلاءه (۱) انظر: التفسير الكبير (۲۳/۱)، بالمعنى. Explanation that He, exalted, guides whom He wills and misguides whom He wills. He guides whom He wills, protects and grants well-being to whom He wills as a favor, and misguides whom He wills, abandons and afflicts as justice. And He is exalted above opposites and rivals. There is no repeller of His decree, no revoker of His judgment, and no overcomer of His command. We believe in all of that, and we are certain that everything is from Him. And He, glorified, (guides) to good whomever He wills (His guidance). Imam al-Razi said in al-Tafsir al-Kabir: Guidance is the indication of what leads to the desired end, whether it actually leads or not; for it is used in both meanings, as in His saying: (Indeed, you do not guide whom you love) [Surat al-Qasas, verse 56] and His saying: (And as for Thamud, We guided them) [Surat Fussilat, verse 17]. But the usage in the sense of leading guidance is more common; for this reason, the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah defined it as creating the act of being guided (1) end quote. And in al-Kashshaf: It is the leading guidance to the desired end (3). Al-Razi objected to it, and some refuted his objections and some refuted those refutations, and I have not seen benefit in presenting them because they are merely dialectical and claims. (And He protects) whom He wills with protection, which is a faculty that impels its possessor to avoid sins while being capable of them. As-Sayyid said (3). (And He grants well-being) i.e., He repels from whom He wills His well-being, which is Allah's defense of the servant. Mukhtar (1). (As a favor) from Him and a bounty. (And He misguides) whom He wills with misguidance, which is the opposite of right guidance. (And He abandons) - with damma on the dhal - He withholds His victory and assistance. (And He afflicts) with evil whom He wills of those whom He abandons and afflicts. (1) See: al-Tafsir al-Kabir (23/1), paraphrased. (2) al-Kashshaf (116/1) (3) al-Ta'rifat p. 131. (4) Mukhtar al-Sihah, entry (ع ف ا).
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the creedal statement about God's guidance and misguidance. It begins by quoting the creed: He guides, protects, and grants well-being as favor, and misguides, abandons, and afflicts as justice. It asserts God's transcendence above opposites and rivals, and the irresistibility of His decree. Then it provides definitions. For guidance (الهداية), it cites Imam al-Razi: guidance is indication (الدلالة) of what leads to the desired end, whether it actually leads or not, as shown in two Quranic verses. It notes that the more common usage is leading guidance (الدلالة الموصلة), which the early Sunni scholars defined as 'creating the act of being guided' (خلق الاهتداء). The commentary from al-Kashshaf defines it as leading guidance. It mentions al-Razi's objection to al-Kashshaf's definition and subsequent debates, but the author says he sees no benefit in detailing them. Then it defines protection (العصمة) as a faculty (ملكة) that prevents its possessor from committing sins while having the ability. It defines well-being (العافية) as God's defense (دفاع) of the servant. It then clarifies that misguidance (الإضلال) is the opposite of right guidance, and abandonment (الخذلان) is withholding victory and assistance. Affliction (الابتلاء) is with evil. The footnote references the sources. This passage covers both the doctrinal statement and the technical definitions of key terms.

?

Defining Divine Guidance, Protection, and Affliction
Scholarly definitions of key divine attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the technical definitions of guidance, protection, and well-being as per Sunni scholars, and the meaning of misguidance and abandonment.

Core Idea
Guidance is leading indication; protection is a faculty against sin; well-being is divine defense.

After affirming the creed, the author elaborates on the key terms, drawing from major tafsir and word definitions. These definitions clarify that guidance is not mere information but effective leading, and protection is an inner quality from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of guidance
Read al-Razi's definition and the Sunni definition. Note the distinction between indicative and leading guidance.
The early Sunni definition is 'creating the act of being guided'.
2
Understand the scholarly dispute
Notice the brief mention of al-Razi's objection to al-Kashshaf. The author considers it unhelpful.
3
Learn the definition of protection
Protection (عصمة) is defined as a faculty that enables avoidance of sins while capable of them.
4
Learn the definition of well-being
Well-being (عافية) is defined as God's defense of the servant.
5
Understand misguidance and abandonment
Misguidance is the opposite of right guidance; abandonment is withholding support; affliction is with evil.

بيان أنه تعالى يهدي من يشاء ويضل من يشاء] يَهْدِي مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَيَعْصِمُ وَيُعَافِي مَنْ يَشَاءُ فَضْلًا، وَيُضِلُّ مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَيَخْذُلُ ويبتلي عَدْلًا، وَهُوَ مُتَعَالٍ عَنِ الأَضْدَادِ وَالأَنْدَادِ، لَا رَادَّ لِقَضَائِهِ وَلَا مُعَقِّبَ حُكْمِهِ وَلَا غَالِبَ لِأَمْرِهِ، آمَنَّا بِذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ، وَأَيْقَنَّا أَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْ عِنْدِهِ. وهو سبحانه ( يهدي) إلى الخير من يشاء ) هدايته، قال الإمام الرازي في التفسير الكبير: الهداية هي الدلالة على ما يوصل إلى المطلوب أوصل إليه بالفعل أو لا؛ فإنها مستعملة في كلا المعنيين كما في قوله تعالى: (إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِى مَنْ أحببت) (سورة القصص آية: ٥٦) وقوله تعالى: (وَأَمَّا ثَمُودُ فَهَدَيْنَهُمْ﴾ [سورة فصلت آية : ۱۷]، لكن الاستعمال في معنى الدلالة الموصلة أكثر؛ ولهذا عرفها المتقدمون من مشايخ أهل السنة بخلق الاهتداء (١) اهـ. و في الكشاف: هي الدلالة الموصلة إلى المطلوب (۳).واعترض عليه الرازي، ودفع بعضهم اعتراضاته وبعضهم دفع دفعها، ولم أر في إيرادها جدوى لكونها مدافعة ودعوى سرى ( ويعصم) من يشاء عصمته، وهي ملكة تحمل صاحبها على اجتناب المعاصي مع التمكن منها. قاله السيد (۳). (ويعاني) أي يدفع عن من يشاء) عافيته، وهي دفاع الله تعالى عن العبد. مختار (1) (فضلا) منه ومنة، ويضل من يشاء) إضلاله، وهو ضد الرشاد، (ويخذل) - بضم -الذال يترك نصرته وعونه ( ويبتلي) بالشر من يشاء خذلانه وابتلاءه (۱) انظر: التفسير الكبير (۲۳/۱)، بالمعنى. Explanation that He, exalted, guides whom He wills and misguides whom He wills. He guides whom He wills, protects and grants well-being to whom He wills as a favor, and misguides whom He wills, abandons and afflicts as justice. And He is exalted above opposites and rivals. There is no repeller of His decree, no revoker of His judgment, and no overcomer of His command. We believe in all of that, and we are certain that everything is from Him. And He, glorified, (guides) to good whomever He wills (His guidance). Imam al-Razi said in al-Tafsir al-Kabir: Guidance is the indication of what leads to the desired end, whether it actually leads or not; for it is used in both meanings, as in His saying: (Indeed, you do not guide whom you love) [Surat al-Qasas, verse 56] and His saying: (And as for Thamud, We guided them) [Surat Fussilat, verse 17]. But the usage in the sense of leading guidance is more common; for this reason, the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah defined it as creating the act of being guided (1) end quote. And in al-Kashshaf: It is the leading guidance to the desired end (3). Al-Razi objected to it, and some refuted his objections and some refuted those refutations, and I have not seen benefit in presenting them because they are merely dialectical and claims. (And He protects) whom He wills with protection, which is a faculty that impels its possessor to avoid sins while being capable of them. As-Sayyid said (3). (And He grants well-being) i.e., He repels from whom He wills His well-being, which is Allah's defense of the servant. Mukhtar (1). (As a favor) from Him and a bounty. (And He misguides) whom He wills with misguidance, which is the opposite of right guidance. (And He abandons) - with damma on the dhal - He withholds His victory and assistance. (And He afflicts) with evil whom He wills of those whom He abandons and afflicts. (1) See: al-Tafsir al-Kabir (23/1), paraphrased. (2) al-Kashshaf (116/1) (3) al-Ta'rifat p. 131. (4) Mukhtar al-Sihah, entry (ع ف ا).
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the creedal statement about God's guidance and misguidance. It begins by quoting the creed: He guides, protects, and grants well-being as favor, and misguides, abandons, and afflicts as justice. It asserts God's transcendence above opposites and rivals, and the irresistibility of His decree. Then it provides definitions. For guidance (الهداية), it cites Imam al-Razi: guidance is indication (الدلالة) of what leads to the desired end, whether it actually leads or not, as shown in two Quranic verses. It notes that the more common usage is leading guidance (الدلالة الموصلة), which the early Sunni scholars defined as 'creating the act of being guided' (خلق الاهتداء). The commentary from al-Kashshaf defines it as leading guidance. It mentions al-Razi's objection to al-Kashshaf's definition and subsequent debates, but the author says he sees no benefit in detailing them. Then it defines protection (العصمة) as a faculty (ملكة) that prevents its possessor from committing sins while having the ability. It defines well-being (العافية) as God's defense (دفاع) of the servant. It then clarifies that misguidance (الإضلال) is the opposite of right guidance, and abandonment (الخذلان) is withholding victory and assistance. Affliction (الابتلاء) is with evil. The footnote references the sources. This passage covers both the doctrinal statement and the technical definitions of key terms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage defines guidance as 'creating the act of being guided.' If your faith is entirely a creation of Allah in you, not your own achievement, then why do you sometimes feel proud of your religious deeds? Will you thank Him right now for giving you even the desire to seek Him?
?
Protection (عصمة) is described as a faculty that impels you to avoid sin while you are still capable of committing it. Think of a sin you fell into—was it because Allah withheld that faculty from you at that moment? How does that realization make you depend on Him for every breath you do not sin?
?
Affliction (ابتلاء) is linked to divine abandonment and trial. When you face hardship, do you instinctively assume Allah has abandoned you, or do you see it as a test that requires patience? What concrete change in your attitude toward a current difficulty does this definition demand right now?

The Two Circles of Mercy and Wisdom
Al-Haddad and commentator explain the two circles of mercy and wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah's attributes of mercy and wisdom are manifested in creation and the afterlife, and how every creature is placed in one of two circles.

Core Idea
Every creature is either in the circle of mercy or the circle of wisdom, leading to bounty or justice.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah commentary introduces a profound framework for understanding divine decree: two circles that encompass all creation. The gnostic al-Haddad presents the aphorism that sets the stage, and the commentator elaborates on how Allah's eternal attributes divide humanity into two groups. As you read, notice how mercy and wisdom are not opposites but complementary aspects of Allah's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the aphorism and explanation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Focus on the two circles mentioned in the aphorism and how the commentator explains them.
2
Identify the two circles and their outcomes
Notice that those in the circle of mercy receive bounty, while those in the circle of wisdom receive justice. See how the commentator links these to Allah's eternal attributes.
3
Reflect on the balance of mercy and justice
Consider how the passage shows that all people are subject to both mercy and wisdom, but one predominates. The moral is to praise Allah for guidance and blame oneself for harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(عدلا) منه، ونقمة، قال العارف السيد عبدالله الحداد (۱) في حكمه: «الخلق مع الحق لا يخلو أحد منهم أن يكون في إحدى الدائرتين؛ إما في دائرة الرحمة أو في دائرة الحكمة؛ فمن كان اليوم في دائرة الرحمة كان غدًا في دائرة الفضل، ومن كان اليوم في دائرة الحكمة كان غدًا في دائرة العدل» اهـ. قال شارحها: «وجل هذا المقام أن الله تعالى كان موصوفًا في الأزل بأوصاف الرحمة؛ كالجود والكرم والرأفة واللطف والإحسان، وموصوفًا بصفات النقمة؛ كالقهر والإضلال والانتقام؛ فقسم خلقه بإرادته قسمين؛ فمنهم من قسم لهم أن يكونوا مظاهر أوصاف الرحمة في الأغلب وإن كانوا لا يخلون عن الحكمة والعدل، ومنهم من قسم لهم أن يكونوا مظاهر صفات النقمة المشتملة على الحكمة في الأغلب وإن كانوا لا يخلون عن الرحمة والفضل، ثم أخرجهم من العدم إلى فضاء الوجود فسهل لكل ما قسم له، ثم إذا أوردهم في مورد القيامة جعل أهل دائرة الرحمة بفضله في آلاء لا تحصى، وجعل أهل دائرة الحكمة بعدله في بلايا لا تقصى؛ فمن وفقه الله للخير فلا يحمدون إلا إياه ومن ابتلي بالضير فلا يلومن إلا نفسه» اهـ.
('Justice from Him, and vengeance.') The gnostic Sayyid 'Abdullah al-Haddad (1) said in his aphorisms: 'Creation with the Truth is such that none of them is except in one of two circles: either in the circle of mercy or in the circle of wisdom. So whoever is today in the circle of mercy will be tomorrow in the circle of bounty, and whoever is today in the circle of wisdom will be tomorrow in the circle of justice.' End quote. The commentator said: 'And the greatness of this station is that Allah, exalted, was described in pre-eternity with attributes of mercy, such as munificence, generosity, compassion, kindness, and beneficence, and described with attributes of vengeance, such as subjugation, misguidance, and retaliation. So He divided His creation by His will into two groups: among them are those whom He apportioned to be manifestations of the attributes of mercy predominantly, though they are not free from wisdom and justice; and among them are those whom He apportioned to be manifestations of the attributes of vengeance, which include wisdom, predominantly, though they are not free from mercy and bounty. Then He brought them forth from non-existence into the expanse of existence and facilitated for each what was apportioned for him. Then, when He brings them to the place of resurrection, He makes the people of the circle of mercy, by His bounty, in blessings without number, and He makes the people of the circle of wisdom, by His justice, in trials without end. So whoever Allah grants success to good, they should praise none but Him, and whoever is afflicted with harm, he should blame none but himself.' End quote.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a phrase from the Tahawiyyah, likely 'عدلا منه ونقمة' (justice from Him, and vengeance). The commentator first quotes the gnostic 'Abdullah al-Haddad, who states that every creature is in one of two circles with respect to Allah: the circle of mercy or the circle of wisdom. Those in the circle of mercy today will receive bounty tomorrow, while those in the circle of wisdom today will encounter justice tomorrow. The commentator then expands on this idea. He explains that Allah from pre-eternity possessed attributes of mercy (like generosity, kindness, and beneficence) and attributes of vengeance (like subjugation, misguidance, and retaliation). By His will, He divided His creation into two groups: one group was destined to be manifestations of the attributes of mercy predominantly, though they still have a share of wisdom and justice; the other group was destined to be manifestations of the attributes of vengeance, which include wisdom, predominantly, though they also have a share of mercy and bounty. Allah then brought them into existence and made easy for each what was decreed for them. On the Day of Resurrection, He will place the people of mercy in endless blessings by His bounty, and the people of wisdom in endless trials by His justice. The passage concludes with a moral: whoever is guided to good should praise only Allah, and whoever is afflicted with harm should blame only himself. This reinforces the Sunni doctrine of divine predestination and human responsibility.

صفات النقمة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's mercy and justice are in conflict.
Correction: The passage shows that both are perfectly manifested in creation and decree; they are complementary, not contradictory.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what are the two circles in which every creature finds themselves?
A) The circle of bounty and the circle of justice
B) The circle of mercy and the circle of wisdom
C) The circle of pleasure and the circle of punishment
D) The circle of good and the circle of evil

Key Takeaway
Allah's decree is perfectly just and merciful, with every creature placed in one of two circles that determine their ultimate outcome.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which circle do you honestly believe you are in today? If you are experiencing ease and blessings, do you attribute it to your own worth or to Allah's sheer mercy? If you are facing trials, do you blame yourself entirely, or do you recognize Allah's wisdom in placing you there? How does this awareness change your gratitude or patience right now?
?
The passage says: 'Whoever Allah grants success to good, they should praise none but Him.' Think of a recent good deed or success. When you succeeded, did you feel pride in your own effort, or did you genuinely thank Allah as the sole giver? What would it take for you to internalize that every good in your life is from Him alone?
?
Consider a harm or failure you have experienced. The commentator says: 'whoever is afflicted with harm, he should blame none but himself.' Do you truly accept that your own action (or inaction) is the cause, or do you secretly resent Allah's decree? How can you reconcile this blame with the belief that everything happens by Allah's will? What step can you take today to embrace both your responsibility and His sovereignty?

The Quran is the Uncreated Speech of Allah
Affirms the Quran as uncreated speech and refutes those who deny it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech, beginning without modality, and that denying this constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not created like human words.

This lesson establishes the foundational creed regarding the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah. Imam al-Tahawi affirms that the Quran is Allah's speech that began without modality, and he clearly states that anyone who claims it is human speech falls into disbelief. The passage also provides evidence from the Quran itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the core creedal statement
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the text declares the Quran to be the speech of Allah, beginning without modality (bila kayfiyya).
The phrase 'bada'a bila kayfiyya' emphasizes that we do not ask how it began.
2
Identify the key claim and its consequence
Find where the text says that hearing the Quran and claiming it is human speech leads to disbelief. Understand the gravity of this statement.
3
Reflect on the Quranic proof
The passage quotes Quran 74:26 and 74:25. See how Allah threatens those who call the Quran human speech with Saqar, confirming the Quran is the Creator's speech.
This verse is a direct proof from scripture.

الكلام في معجزته القرآن
وَإِنَّ القُرْآنَ كَلَامُ الله تَعَالَى بَدَأَ بِلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ قَوْلًا وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ وَحْيَا وَصَدَّقَهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ حَقًّا، وَأَبْقَنُوا أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِالْحَقِيقَةِ لَيْسَ بِمَخْلُوقٍ كَكَلَامِ البَرِيَّةِ؛ فَمَنْ سَمِعَهُ فَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ، وَقَدْ ذَمَّهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَابَهُ وَأَوْعَدَهُ عَذَابَهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: سَأَصْلِيهِ سَفَرَ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٦] فَلَمَّا أَوْعَدَ اللهُ سَقَرَ لَنْ قَالَ: إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ ) (سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] عَلِمْنَا أَنَّهُ قَوْلُ خَالِقِ البَشَرِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُ قَوْلَ البَشَرِ .
وَمَنْ وَصَفَ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِمَعْنَى مِنْ مَعَانِي البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ؛ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ هَذَا اعْتَبَرَ
وَعَنْ مِثْلِ قَوْلِ الكُفَّارِ انْزَجَرَ ، وَعَلِمَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِصِفَاتِهِ لَيْسَ كَالْبَشَرِ.
(و) نقول: (إن القرآن) أي ( كلام الله تعالى) الذي بدأ) أي ظهر منه لنا (بلا كيفية) نتعقلها من حرف أو صوت أو بدء أو سكوت، والجار والمجرور حال مــن قوله (قولا) أي معقولا بلا كيفية، وأنزله على نبيه) (وحيا) أي بواسطته، وصدقه المؤمنون على ذلك كله تصديقا (حقا، وأيقنوا أنه أي القرآن والمراد به المقروء (كلام الله تعالى بالحقيقة). وهو (١) الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته تعالى المنافية للسكوت والآفة وليس بحرف ولا صوت ليس بمخلوق ككلام البرية المؤلف من الحروف المشتمل على الأصوات، وقوله: «ليس بمخلوق خبر لقوله: «إن القرآن»؛ ولذا جعلت قوله كلام الله تفسيرًا للقرآن، وإن كان الأقرب أن يكون هو الخبر؛ لما نقل السعد في شرح العقائد عن الأشياخ أنه يقال : القرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ولا
Discussion of his miracle: the Quran. And indeed the Quran is the speech of Allah Most High, He began it without modality as speech, and sent it down to His Prophet as revelation, and the believers affirmed it regarding that truthfully, and they were certain that it is the speech of Allah Most High in reality, not created like the speech of creatures; so whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has disbelieved, and Allah has blamed him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment, where He said: 'I will burn him in Saqar' [Quran 74:26]. So when Allah threatened with Saqar for the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of a human' [Quran 74:25], we knew that it is the speech of the Creator of humans and does not resemble the speech of humans. And whoever describes Allah Most High with a meaning from the meanings of humans has disbelieved; so whoever perceives this will take heed and be deterred from the like of the speech of the disbelievers, and know that Allah Most High, with His attributes, is not like humans. And we say: 'Indeed the Quran' — i.e., the speech of Allah Most High — 'He began' i.e., it appeared to us — 'without modality' that we can comprehend of letter, sound, beginning, or silence, and the prepositional phrase is an adverbial from His saying 'as speech' i.e., understood without modality, and sent it down upon His Prophet 'as revelation' i.e., through His mediation, and the believers affirmed all that with true affirmation and were certain that it — i.e., the Quran, meaning the recited — is the speech of Allah Most High in reality. And it (i.e., the speech of Allah) is the eternal attribute subsisting with His essence, negating silence and defect, and it is not a letter nor a sound, not created like the speech of creatures composed of letters containing sounds. And His saying 'not created' is the predicate of His saying 'Indeed the Quran', and therefore His saying 'speech of Allah' was made an interpretation of 'Quran', although the closer is that it is the predicate; according to what Sa'd reported in Sharh al-'Aqa'id from the masters, it is said: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, not created, and not...'
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the nature of the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah, followed by a grammatical explanation of the creedal statement. It begins with a heading: 'Discussion of his miracle: the Quran.' Then it presents the Tahawiyyah creed text affirming that the Quran is Allah's speech, beginning without modality (bila kayfiyya), sent down as revelation. Believers affirm this and know it is not created like human speech. Anyone who claims it is human speech commits disbelief, and Allah threatens such a person with Saqar, citing Quran 74:26-25. The passage then adds an independent ruling: describing Allah with anthropomorphic meanings leads to disbelief. It then provides a detailed commentary on the phrase 'Inna al-Qur'ana kalam Allah ta'ala'. The commentator explains that 'bada'a' means 'appeared to us' and 'bila kayfiyya' means without modality that we can comprehend (letter, sound, beginning, silence). The phrase 'qawlan' is explained as 'understood without modality'. The revelation is through Jibril. Then it clarifies that the Quran is the eternal attribute (al-sifa al-azaliyya) subsisting with Allah's essence, which negates silence and defect; it is not letters or sounds, and is not created. The commentary then discusses grammatical analysis: 'laysa bi makhluqin' is the predicate of 'inna al-qur'ana', and 'kalam Allah' is an interpretation (tafsir) of 'al-Qur'an', though the closer view is that 'kalam Allah' is the predicate. This is supported by a report from Sa'd al-Taftazani in his commentary on 'Aqa'id al-Nasafi that the masters (ashyakh) say: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, not created, and not...' The text ends abruptly with 'wa la' (and not...), presumably continuing to negate being created.

كلام الله
بدا
لا كيفية
مخلوق

Misconception: Some think the Quran is created or merely figurative speech.
Correction: The passage clearly states the Quran is not created like the speech of creatures, and claiming it is human speech is disbelief.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah; denying this is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Eternal Attribute of Speech and Its Nature
Explains the Quran as eternal attribute and refutes anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, and that describing Allah with human attributes leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, not created, and unlike human speech.

This lesson delves into the theological explanation of the Quran as Allah's eternal attribute. It clarifies that the Quran is not letters or sounds, and that any anthropomorphism leads to disbelief. The passage also includes a grammatical analysis of the creedal statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling on anthropomorphism
The passage begins with a strong statement: describing Allah with human meanings is disbelief. Read this and understand its consequence.
2
Analyze the nature of Allah's speech
The text explains that the Quran is the eternal attribute (al-sifa al-azaliyya) subsisting with Allah's essence, negating silence and defect. It is not a letter or sound.
This refutes those who think the Quran is created or composed of letters.
3
Examine the grammatical structure
The commentary discusses whether 'kalam Allah' is the predicate or an interpretation of 'al-Qur'an'. Consider the importance of precise theological language.
The reference to al-Sa'd in Sharh al-'Aqa'id shows the traditional view.

الكلام في معجزته القرآن
وَإِنَّ القُرْآنَ كَلَامُ الله تَعَالَى بَدَأَ بِلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ قَوْلًا وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ وَحْيَا وَصَدَّقَهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ حَقًّا، وَأَبْقَنُوا أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِالْحَقِيقَةِ لَيْسَ بِمَخْلُوقٍ كَكَلَامِ البَرِيَّةِ؛ فَمَنْ سَمِعَهُ فَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ، وَقَدْ ذَمَّهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَابَهُ وَأَوْعَدَهُ عَذَابَهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: سَأَصْلِيهِ سَفَرَ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٦] فَلَمَّا أَوْعَدَ اللهُ سَقَرَ لَنْ قَالَ: إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ ) (سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] عَلِمْنَا أَنَّهُ قَوْلُ خَالِقِ البَشَرِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُ قَوْلَ البَشَرِ .
وَمَنْ وَصَفَ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِمَعْنَى مِنْ مَعَانِي البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ؛ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ هَذَا اعْتَبَرَ
وَعَنْ مِثْلِ قَوْلِ الكُفَّارِ انْزَجَرَ ، وَعَلِمَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِصِفَاتِهِ لَيْسَ كَالْبَشَرِ.
(و) نقول: (إن القرآن) أي ( كلام الله تعالى) الذي بدأ) أي ظهر منه لنا (بلا كيفية) نتعقلها من حرف أو صوت أو بدء أو سكوت، والجار والمجرور حال مــن قوله (قولا) أي معقولا بلا كيفية، وأنزله على نبيه) (وحيا) أي بواسطته، وصدقه المؤمنون على ذلك كله تصديقا (حقا، وأيقنوا أنه أي القرآن والمراد به المقروء (كلام الله تعالى بالحقيقة). وهو (١) الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته تعالى المنافية للسكوت والآفة وليس بحرف ولا صوت ليس بمخلوق ككلام البرية المؤلف من الحروف المشتمل على الأصوات، وقوله: «ليس بمخلوق خبر لقوله: «إن القرآن»؛ ولذا جعلت قوله كلام الله تفسيرًا للقرآن، وإن كان الأقرب أن يكون هو الخبر؛ لما نقل السعد في شرح العقائد عن الأشياخ أنه يقال : القرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ولا
Discussion of his miracle: the Quran. And indeed the Quran is the speech of Allah Most High, He began it without modality as speech, and sent it down to His Prophet as revelation, and the believers affirmed it regarding that truthfully, and they were certain that it is the speech of Allah Most High in reality, not created like the speech of creatures; so whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has disbelieved, and Allah has blamed him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment, where He said: 'I will burn him in Saqar' [Quran 74:26]. So when Allah threatened with Saqar for the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of a human' [Quran 74:25], we knew that it is the speech of the Creator of humans and does not resemble the speech of humans. And whoever describes Allah Most High with a meaning from the meanings of humans has disbelieved; so whoever perceives this will take heed and be deterred from the like of the speech of the disbelievers, and know that Allah Most High, with His attributes, is not like humans. And we say: 'Indeed the Quran' — i.e., the speech of Allah Most High — 'He began' i.e., it appeared to us — 'without modality' that we can comprehend of letter, sound, beginning, or silence, and the prepositional phrase is an adverbial from His saying 'as speech' i.e., understood without modality, and sent it down upon His Prophet 'as revelation' i.e., through His mediation, and the believers affirmed all that with true affirmation and were certain that it — i.e., the Quran, meaning the recited — is the speech of Allah Most High in reality. And it (i.e., the speech of Allah) is the eternal attribute subsisting with His essence, negating silence and defect, and it is not a letter nor a sound, not created like the speech of creatures composed of letters containing sounds. And His saying 'not created' is the predicate of His saying 'Indeed the Quran', and therefore His saying 'speech of Allah' was made an interpretation of 'Quran', although the closer is that it is the predicate; according to what Sa'd reported in Sharh al-'Aqa'id from the masters, it is said: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, not created, and not...'
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the nature of the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah, followed by a grammatical explanation of the creedal statement. It begins with a heading: 'Discussion of his miracle: the Quran.' Then it presents the Tahawiyyah creed text affirming that the Quran is Allah's speech, beginning without modality (bila kayfiyya), sent down as revelation. Believers affirm this and know it is not created like human speech. Anyone who claims it is human speech commits disbelief, and Allah threatens such a person with Saqar, citing Quran 74:26-25. The passage then adds an independent ruling: describing Allah with anthropomorphic meanings leads to disbelief. It then provides a detailed commentary on the phrase 'Inna al-Qur'ana kalam Allah ta'ala'. The commentator explains that 'bada'a' means 'appeared to us' and 'bila kayfiyya' means without modality that we can comprehend (letter, sound, beginning, silence). The phrase 'qawlan' is explained as 'understood without modality'. The revelation is through Jibril. Then it clarifies that the Quran is the eternal attribute (al-sifa al-azaliyya) subsisting with Allah's essence, which negates silence and defect; it is not letters or sounds, and is not created. The commentary then discusses grammatical analysis: 'laysa bi makhluqin' is the predicate of 'inna al-qur'ana', and 'kalam Allah' is an interpretation (tafsir) of 'al-Qur'an', though the closer view is that 'kalam Allah' is the predicate. This is supported by a report from Sa'd al-Taftazani in his commentary on 'Aqa'id al-Nasafi that the masters (ashyakh) say: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, not created, and not...' The text ends abruptly with 'wa la' (and not...), presumably continuing to negate being created.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah's speech is composed of letters and sounds like human speech.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the Quran is the eternal attribute, not a letter or sound, and not created.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Quran in relation to Allah?
A) A created thing.
B) An eternal attribute.
C) Human speech.
D) A letter or sound.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal, uncreated attribute, not composed of letters or sounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran is the eternal, uncreated speech of Allah—not composed of letters or sounds—what does that mean for how you approach reading a physical copy? Do you treat it as an attribute of Allah made manifest, or merely as a book among books? How would your concentration change if you truly believed each verse is directly from His eternal attribute?
?
The passage states that describing Allah with human meanings is disbelief. Have you ever, even for a moment, imagined Allah's speech like a human voice? How will you actively guard your thoughts to avoid such anthropomorphism, especially during recitation?
?
If the Quran is 'without modality', it transcends your comprehension. Does that humble you or frustrate you? Will you accept that the true nature of Allah's speech is beyond your intellect, or will you insist on trying to grasp it? What change in your heart is needed to submit to this mystery?

Divine Attributes

The Quran is Uncreated Speech: The Core Belief
Maydani states the creed that the Quran is uncreated speech without modality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational creed that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, and the proper way to affirm it without modality.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not created like human speech.

In this passage, Imam al-Maydani begins by presenting the foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunnah: the Quran is the speech of Allah in reality, uncreated and revealed without modality. This sets the stage for understanding why denying this is kufr and how to maintain tanzih.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noticing the key phrase 'bila kayfiyyah' and the affirmation that the Quran is not created like the speech of creatures.
2
Identify the components of the creed
Note the four elements: the Quran as speech of Allah, its beginning without modality, its revelation, and the believers' certainty.
3
Understand 'bila kayfiyyah'
Reflect on why the Salaf avoided specifying how Allah speaks, and what this means for our belief about the Quran.
This is a key principle of tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّ القُرْآنَ كَلَامُ الله تَعَالَى بَدَأَ بِلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ قَوْلًا وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ وَحْيَا وَصَدَّقَهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ حَقًّا، وَأَبْقَنُوا أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِالْحَقِيقَةِ لَيْسَ بِمَخْلُوقٍ كَكَلَامِ البَرِيَّةِ؛ فَمَنْ سَمِعَهُ فَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ، وَقَدْ ذَمَّهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَابَهُ وَأَوْعَدَهُ عَذَابَهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: سَأَصْلِيهِ سَقَرَ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٦] فَلَمَّا أَوْعَدَ اللهُ سَقَرَ لِمَنْ قَالَ: إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ ) (سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] عَلِمْنَا أَنَّهُ قَوْلُ خَالِقِ البَشَرِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُ قَوْلَ البَشَرِ . وَمَنْ وَصَفَ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِمَعْنَى مِنْ مَعَانِي البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ؛ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ هَذَا اعْتَبَرَ وَعَنْ مِثْلِ قَوْلِ الكُفَّارِ انْزَجَرَ ، وَعَلِمَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِصِفَاتِهِ لَيْسَ كَالْبَشَرِ. (و) نقول: (إن القرآن) أي ( كلام الله تعالى) الذي بدأ) أي ظهر منه لنا (بلا كيفية) نتعقلها من حرف أو صوت أو بدء أو سكوت، والجار والمجرور حال مــن قوله (قولا) أي معقولا بلا كيفية، وأنزله على نبيه) (وحيا) أي بواسطته، وصدقه المؤمنون على ذلك كله تصديقا (حقا، وأيقنوا أنه أي القرآن والمراد به المقروء (كلام الله تعالى بالحقيقة). وهو (١) الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته تعالى المنافية للسكوت والآفة وليس بحرف ولا صوت ليس بمخلوق ككلام البرية المؤلف من الحروف المشتمل على الأصوات، وقوله: «ليس بمخلوق خبر لقوله: «إن القرآن»؛ ولذا جعلت قوله كلام الله تفسيرًا للقرآن، وإن كان الأقرب أن يكون هو الخبر؛ لما نقل السعد في شرح العقائد عن الأشياخ أنه يقال : القرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ولا يقال: القرآن غير مخلوق؛ لئلا يسبق إلى الفهم أن المؤلف من الأصوات والحروف قديم كما ذهب إليه الحنابلة جهلا أو عنادا ) (۲) اهـ . فمن سمعه فزعم أنه كلام البشر فقد افترى على الله تعالى و (كفر؛ و) ذلك لأنه قد ذمه الله تعالى وعابه وأوعده) انتقامه و عذابه) ؛ وما ذلك إلا لافترانه على ربه بنسبة صفته القديمة إلى خلقه وذلك حيث قال تعالى في شأنه (( سَأُصْلِيهِ سَقَر [سورة المدثر آية : ٢٦]؛ فلما أوعد الله تعالى (سقر لمن قال: إنْ هَذَا )) أي القرآن (إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ ) (سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] علمنا أنه قول خالق البشر ، و ( قول الخالق ( لا يشبه قـول البشر )؛ تعالى الله أن تماثل صفاته وتكبر. ومن) وصف الله تعالى بمعنى من معاني البشر فقد ضل و (كفر) واستوجب العذاب الأكبر، فمن أبصر (هذا وتدبر وعلم ما في الجرأة على الله من الخطر تنبه واعتبر، وعن مثل قول الكفار انزجر، وعلم أن الله تعالى بصفاته كلها ليس كالبشر.
And indeed the Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Exalted, which began without modality as speech, and He revealed it to His Prophet as revelation, and the believers affirmed it upon that truly, and they were certain that it is the speech of Allah the Exalted in reality, not created like the speech of creation; so whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has indeed disbelieved, and Allah the Exalted has condemned him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment where He said: 'I will roast him in Saqar' [Surah al-Muddaththir: 26]. So when Allah threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of humans' [Surah al-Muddaththir: 25], we knew that it is the speech of the Creator of humans and does not resemble human speech. And whoever describes Allah the Exalted with a meaning from the meanings of humans has disbelieved; so whoever perceives this takes heed and refrains from the like of the saying of the disbelievers, and knows that Allah the Exalted in His attributes is not like humans. (And) we say: 'Indeed the Qur'an' i.e. the speech of Allah the Exalted which began i.e. appeared to us without modality which we conceive of letter or sound or beginning or silence, and the prepositional phrase is hal from His saying 'speech' i.e. understood without modality, and He revealed it to His Prophet as revelation i.e. by its means, and the believers affirmed all of that as true affirmation, and they were certain that it i.e. the Qur'an, meaning the recited, is the speech of Allah the Exalted in reality. And it is the eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, incompatible with silence and defect, and it is not a letter nor a sound, not created like the speech of creation composed of letters containing sounds. And His saying 'not created' is the predicate of His saying 'Indeed the Qur'an'; and therefore His saying 'speech of Allah' was made an interpretation of 'the Qur'an', although the closer view is that it is the predicate; because al-Sa'd transmitted in Sharh al-'Aqa'id from the shaykhs that it is said: 'The Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Exalted, uncreated,' and it is not said: 'The Qur'an is uncreated,' lest it should come to mind that what is composed of sounds and letters is eternal, as the Hanbalis held out of ignorance or obstinacy. So whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has indeed fabricated against Allah the Exalted and disbelieved; and that is because Allah the Exalted has condemned him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment and penalty; and that is only due to his fabrication against his Lord by attributing His eternal attribute to His creation, and that is where the Exalted said concerning him: 'I will roast him in Saqar'; so when Allah the Exalted threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of humans,' we knew that it is the speech of the Creator of humans, and the speech of the Creator does not resemble human speech; exalted is Allah that His attributes should be similar and magnified. And whoever describes Allah the Exalted with a meaning from the meanings of humans has indeed gone astray and disbelieved and incurs the greater punishment; so whoever perceives this and reflects and knows the danger in daring against Allah becomes alert and takes heed, and refrains from the like of the saying of the disbelievers, and knows that Allah the Exalted in all His attributes is not like humans.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-proof passage, where al-Maydani explains and defends the Tahawiyyah creed concerning the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah. The text first presents the core belief: the Quran is the speech of Allah that 'began' (i.e., appeared from Him) without any modality (bila kayfiyyah), meaning we do not conceive of it in terms of letters, sounds, beginning, or silence. It was revealed to the Prophet as revelation. Believers affirm it as truly the speech of Allah in reality, not created like the speech of creatures. The passage then provides a proof from the Quran itself: Allah threatened with Hellfire (Saqar) the one who said 'This is nothing but the speech of humans' (Surah al-Muddaththir 25-26). This threat proves that such a statement is kufr, and therefore the Quran must be the speech of the Creator, unlike human speech. The commentary elaborates on the theological nuance: the Quran is the eternal attribute of speech (sifat kalam nafsi) subsisting in Allah's essence, not composed of letters or sounds, and thus not created. It cautions against saying 'the Quran is uncreated' without qualification, as this might lead to the misconception that the physical letters and sounds are eternal—a view attributed to the Hanbalis out of ignorance or obstinacy. Finally, the passage extends the principle: whoever describes Allah with human attributes has disbelieved, because Allah's attributes are unlike human attributes. The overall argument follows the Tahawiyyah line: the Quran is divine speech, its denial is kufr, and Allah's attributes are transcendent.

Key Terms
القرآن
كلام الله
بلا كيفية
غير مخلوق
الحقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the phrase 'bada'a' (began) implies the Quran had a temporal beginning as an attribute of Allah.
Correction: The Salaf interpreted 'bada'a' as 'appeared to us' without attributing a beginning to the eternal attribute itself. The Quran as divine speech is eternal.

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'bada'a bila kayfiyyah' (began without modality) mean?
A) The Quran existed eternally in the past without beginning.
B) The Quran appeared from Allah without us conceiving of how.
C) The Quran was created in a manner unknown to us.
D) The Quran is composed of letters and sounds.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is Allah's uncreated speech, affirmed without asking how.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech, how does that change the way you listen to its recitation or read its verses? Will you now approach it with greater awe and humility?
?
Do you ever treat the Quran as if it were just another book, analyzing it like human literature? How can you remind yourself that it is 'كلام الله بالحقيقة' (Allah's speech in reality) and not created like human speech?
?
This lesson teaches that the Quran 'began' without modality (بلا كيفية). Are you willing to submit to truths about Allah that your mind cannot fully grasp, or do you secretly wish for a God you can fully understand?

The Quran is Divine: Proof from Saqar
Maydani cites Quranic proof linking denial of the Quran's divinity to punishment in Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic proof that the Quran is the speech of Allah and not human speech, and why claiming it is human speech is an act of disbelief.

Core Idea
Denying the Quran as divine speech and calling it human earns the threat of Hellfire.

After establishing the creed, al-Maydani provides a powerful proof from the Quran itself: the threat of Saqar for the one who says 'This is nothing but human speech.' This demonstrates that such a statement is kufr, and therefore the Quran must be divine.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
See how al-Maydani uses the conditional: if someone says it is human speech, he disbelieves, and Allah threatens him with Saqar.
2
Analyze the logic
The threat proves the opposite: that the Quran is from the Creator, not resembling human speech. Identify the premise, evidence, and conclusion.
This is a logical deduction from a Quranic warning.

Source Text

وَإِنَّ القُرْآنَ كَلَامُ الله تَعَالَى بَدَأَ بِلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ قَوْلًا وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ وَحْيَا وَصَدَّقَهُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ حَقًّا، وَأَبْقَنُوا أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِالْحَقِيقَةِ لَيْسَ بِمَخْلُوقٍ كَكَلَامِ البَرِيَّةِ؛ فَمَنْ سَمِعَهُ فَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ كَلَامُ البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ، وَقَدْ ذَمَّهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَابَهُ وَأَوْعَدَهُ عَذَابَهُ حَيْثُ قَالَ: سَأَصْلِيهِ سَقَرَ [سورة المدثر آية: ٢٦] فَلَمَّا أَوْعَدَ اللهُ سَقَرَ لِمَنْ قَالَ: إِنْ هَذَا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ ) (سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] عَلِمْنَا أَنَّهُ قَوْلُ خَالِقِ البَشَرِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُ قَوْلَ البَشَرِ . وَمَنْ وَصَفَ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِمَعْنَى مِنْ مَعَانِي البَشَرِ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ؛ فَمَنْ أَبْصَرَ هَذَا اعْتَبَرَ وَعَنْ مِثْلِ قَوْلِ الكُفَّارِ انْزَجَرَ ، وَعَلِمَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى بِصِفَاتِهِ لَيْسَ كَالْبَشَرِ. (و) نقول: (إن القرآن) أي ( كلام الله تعالى) الذي بدأ) أي ظهر منه لنا (بلا كيفية) نتعقلها من حرف أو صوت أو بدء أو سكوت، والجار والمجرور حال مــن قوله (قولا) أي معقولا بلا كيفية، وأنزله على نبيه) (وحيا) أي بواسطته، وصدقه المؤمنون على ذلك كله تصديقا (حقا، وأيقنوا أنه أي القرآن والمراد به المقروء (كلام الله تعالى بالحقيقة). وهو (١) الصفة الأزلية القائمة بذاته تعالى المنافية للسكوت والآفة وليس بحرف ولا صوت ليس بمخلوق ككلام البرية المؤلف من الحروف المشتمل على الأصوات، وقوله: «ليس بمخلوق خبر لقوله: «إن القرآن»؛ ولذا جعلت قوله كلام الله تفسيرًا للقرآن، وإن كان الأقرب أن يكون هو الخبر؛ لما نقل السعد في شرح العقائد عن الأشياخ أنه يقال : القرآن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ولا يقال: القرآن غير مخلوق؛ لئلا يسبق إلى الفهم أن المؤلف من الأصوات والحروف قديم كما ذهب إليه الحنابلة جهلا أو عنادا ) (۲) اهـ . فمن سمعه فزعم أنه كلام البشر فقد افترى على الله تعالى و (كفر؛ و) ذلك لأنه قد ذمه الله تعالى وعابه وأوعده) انتقامه و عذابه) ؛ وما ذلك إلا لافترانه على ربه بنسبة صفته القديمة إلى خلقه وذلك حيث قال تعالى في شأنه (( سَأُصْلِيهِ سَقَر [سورة المدثر آية : ٢٦]؛ فلما أوعد الله تعالى (سقر لمن قال: إنْ هَذَا )) أي القرآن (إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ ) (سورة المدثر آية: ٢٥] علمنا أنه قول خالق البشر ، و ( قول الخالق ( لا يشبه قـول البشر )؛ تعالى الله أن تماثل صفاته وتكبر. ومن) وصف الله تعالى بمعنى من معاني البشر فقد ضل و (كفر) واستوجب العذاب الأكبر، فمن أبصر (هذا وتدبر وعلم ما في الجرأة على الله من الخطر تنبه واعتبر، وعن مثل قول الكفار انزجر، وعلم أن الله تعالى بصفاته كلها ليس كالبشر.
And indeed the Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Exalted, which began without modality as speech, and He revealed it to His Prophet as revelation, and the believers affirmed it upon that truly, and they were certain that it is the speech of Allah the Exalted in reality, not created like the speech of creation; so whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has indeed disbelieved, and Allah the Exalted has condemned him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment where He said: 'I will roast him in Saqar' [Surah al-Muddaththir: 26]. So when Allah threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of humans' [Surah al-Muddaththir: 25], we knew that it is the speech of the Creator of humans and does not resemble human speech. And whoever describes Allah the Exalted with a meaning from the meanings of humans has disbelieved; so whoever perceives this takes heed and refrains from the like of the saying of the disbelievers, and knows that Allah the Exalted in His attributes is not like humans. (And) we say: 'Indeed the Qur'an' i.e. the speech of Allah the Exalted which began i.e. appeared to us without modality which we conceive of letter or sound or beginning or silence, and the prepositional phrase is hal from His saying 'speech' i.e. understood without modality, and He revealed it to His Prophet as revelation i.e. by its means, and the believers affirmed all of that as true affirmation, and they were certain that it i.e. the Qur'an, meaning the recited, is the speech of Allah the Exalted in reality. And it is the eternal attribute subsisting in His Essence, incompatible with silence and defect, and it is not a letter nor a sound, not created like the speech of creation composed of letters containing sounds. And His saying 'not created' is the predicate of His saying 'Indeed the Qur'an'; and therefore His saying 'speech of Allah' was made an interpretation of 'the Qur'an', although the closer view is that it is the predicate; because al-Sa'd transmitted in Sharh al-'Aqa'id from the shaykhs that it is said: 'The Qur'an is the speech of Allah the Exalted, uncreated,' and it is not said: 'The Qur'an is uncreated,' lest it should come to mind that what is composed of sounds and letters is eternal, as the Hanbalis held out of ignorance or obstinacy. So whoever hears it and claims that it is human speech has indeed fabricated against Allah the Exalted and disbelieved; and that is because Allah the Exalted has condemned him, criticized him, and threatened him with His punishment and penalty; and that is only due to his fabrication against his Lord by attributing His eternal attribute to His creation, and that is where the Exalted said concerning him: 'I will roast him in Saqar'; so when Allah the Exalted threatened with Saqar the one who said: 'This is nothing but the speech of humans,' we knew that it is the speech of the Creator of humans, and the speech of the Creator does not resemble human speech; exalted is Allah that His attributes should be similar and magnified. And whoever describes Allah the Exalted with a meaning from the meanings of humans has indeed gone astray and disbelieved and incurs the greater punishment; so whoever perceives this and reflects and knows the danger in daring against Allah becomes alert and takes heed, and refrains from the like of the saying of the disbelievers, and knows that Allah the Exalted in all His attributes is not like humans.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-proof passage, where al-Maydani explains and defends the Tahawiyyah creed concerning the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah. The text first presents the core belief: the Quran is the speech of Allah that 'began' (i.e., appeared from Him) without any modality (bila kayfiyyah), meaning we do not conceive of it in terms of letters, sounds, beginning, or silence. It was revealed to the Prophet as revelation. Believers affirm it as truly the speech of Allah in reality, not created like the speech of creatures. The passage then provides a proof from the Quran itself: Allah threatened with Hellfire (Saqar) the one who said 'This is nothing but the speech of humans' (Surah al-Muddaththir 25-26). This threat proves that such a statement is kufr, and therefore the Quran must be the speech of the Creator, unlike human speech. The commentary elaborates on the theological nuance: the Quran is the eternal attribute of speech (sifat kalam nafsi) subsisting in Allah's essence, not composed of letters or sounds, and thus not created. It cautions against saying 'the Quran is uncreated' without qualification, as this might lead to the misconception that the physical letters and sounds are eternal—a view attributed to the Hanbalis out of ignorance or obstinacy. Finally, the passage extends the principle: whoever describes Allah with human attributes has disbelieved, because Allah's attributes are unlike human attributes. The overall argument follows the Tahawiyyah line: the Quran is divine speech, its denial is kufr, and Allah's attributes are transcendent.

Key Terms
سقر
كلام البشر
كفر
ذم
إيعاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That it is a minor sin or acceptable opinion to say the Quran is human speech.
Correction: The passage clearly states that this claim is kufr and incurs Allah's punishment of Saqar, so it is a major act of disbelief.

Checkpoint
What is the Quranic proof al-Maydani uses to show the Quran is divine speech?
A) The miraculous nature of the Quran.
B) The threat of Saqar for calling it human speech.
C) The consensus of scholars.
D) The historical continuity of revelation.

Key Takeaway
Whoever claims the Quran is human speech is guilty of kufr, as proven by the threat of Saqar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even for a moment, felt that the Quran's words could have been written by a human? What does this verse reveal about the gravity of that thought? Will you now actively fight such whispers by reminding yourself of the threat of Saqar?
?
When you recite or listen to the Quran, do you truly internalize that these are the words of Allah, not like any other speech? What practical change will you make today to treat the Quran with the reverence it demands?
?
If Allah warns that claiming the Quran is human speech leads to eternal punishment, how should that affect your speech about the Quran? What will you do the next time you hear someone casually criticize or doubt the Quran's divine origin?

Divine Attributes

The Quran as Eternal Attribute: Nuance and Warning
Maydani clarifies the Quran's nature as an eternal attribute and warns against anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah position that the Quran is the eternal attribute of Allah and the importance of avoiding anthropomorphic descriptions.

Core Idea
The Quran is an eternal attribute of Allah, not composed of letters or sounds, and Allah's attributes are unlike human attributes.

In this final part, al-Maydani delves into the theological nuance: the Quran is the eternal attribute of speech subsisting in Allah's essence, not letters or sounds. He warns against describing Allah with human attributes, which is kufr, and emphasizes that all of Allah's attributes are incomparable.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Quran as an eternal attribute
Note that the Quran is described as the eternal attribute (al-sifah al-azaliyyah) subsisting in Allah's essence, not composed of letters or sounds.
2
Examine the precaution in phrasing
Al-Maydani explains why one should say 'the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated' rather than merely 'the Quran is uncreated' to avoid implying the letters and sounds are eternal.
This nuance distinguishes Ahl al-Sunnah from the Hanbalis, according to the author.
3
Apply the principle to all attributes
The passage concludes with a general warning: describing Allah with human attributes is kufr; all of Allah's attributes are incomparable.
This upholds the principle of tanzih.

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-proof passage, where al-Maydani explains and defends the Tahawiyyah creed concerning the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah. The text first presents the core belief: the Quran is the speech of Allah that 'began' (i.e., appeared from Him) without any modality (bila kayfiyyah), meaning we do not conceive of it in terms of letters, sounds, beginning, or silence. This threat proves that such a statement is kufr, and therefore the Quran must be the speech of the Creator, unlike human speech. The commentary elaborates on the theological nuance: the Quran is the eternal attribute of speech (sifat kalam nafsi) subsisting in Allah's essence, not composed of letters or sounds, and thus not created. Finally, the passage extends the principle: whoever describes Allah with human attributes has disbelieved, because Allah's attributes are unlike human attributes. The overall argument follows the Tahawiyyah line: the Quran is divine speech, its denial is kufr, and Allah's attributes are transcendent.

Divine Attributes

The Quran is Uncreated and Unlike Human Speech
The author affirms the Quran is uncreated, clarifies a misunderstanding, and refutes those who say it is human speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Tahawi creed's affirmation that the Quran is uncreated, the clarification that this does not imply eternal sounds or letters, and the Quranic proof that refutes those who claim it is human speech.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's eternal attribute, not created; calling it human speech is punishable by Hell.

This lesson presents a foundational doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah: the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah. The text begins with the creedal statement, then prevents a common misunderstanding, then provides a Quranic proof against those who liken it to human speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement and clarification
Read the opening lines where the author affirms 'القرآن غير مخلوق' and immediately clarifies that this does not mean the sounds and letters are eternal, refuting the Hanbali view.
Notice that the author distinguishes between the Quran as divine speech and its physical manifestation.
2
Understand the condemnation
The author states that whoever hears the Quran and claims it is human speech has slandered Allah and disbelieved. Identify the reasoning: because it attributes the eternal attribute to creation.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the citation of Surah al-Muddaththir (25-26). See how Allah threatens with Saqar those who say 'This is nothing but the word of a human.' The author infers that the Quran is the word of the Creator, unlike human speech.
This proof is central: Allah's threat shows the gravity of the claim.
4
Grasp the general principle and warning
The author concludes that describing Allah with any human attribute is misguidance and disbelief. He urges reflection and warns against the speech of disbelievers.
This reinforces that Allah's attributes are incomparable.

شرح العقيدة الطحاوية المسماة ، بيان السنة والجماعة. يقال: القرآن غير مخلوق؛ لئلا يسبق إلى الفهم أن المؤلف من الأصوات والحروف قديم كما ذهب إليه الحنابلة جهلا أو عنادا. فمن سمعه فزعم أنه كلام البشر فقد افترى على الله تعالى وكفر؛ وذلك لأنه قد ذمه الله تعالى وعابه وأوعده انتقامه وعذابه؛ وما ذلك إلا لافترانه على ربه بنسبة صفته القديمة إلى خلقه وذلك حيث قال تعالى في شأنه: سَأُصْلِيهِ سَقَر [سورة المدثر آية: 26]؛ فلما أوعد الله تعالى سقر لمن قال: إنْ هذا إِلَّا قَوْلُ الْبَشَرِ [سورة المدثر آية: 25] علمنا أنه قول خالق البشر، وقول الخالق لا يشبه قول البشر؛ تعالى الله أن تماثل صفاته وتكبر. ومن وصف الله تعالى بمعنى من معاني البشر فقد ضل وكفر واستوجب العذاب الأكبر، فمن أبصر هذا وتدبر وعلم ما في الجرأة على الله من الخطر تنبه واعتبر، وعن مثل قول الكفار انزجر، وعلم أن الله تعالى بصفاته كلها ليس كالبشر.
The explanation of the Tahawiyyah creed, called 'The Statement of the Sunnah and the Community.' It is said: The Quran is uncreated; lest it be understood that the author (considers) the sounds and letters eternal, as the Hanbalis hold, out of ignorance or stubbornness. Whoever hears it and claims it is human speech has slandered Allah Almighty and disbelieved; that is because Allah Almighty has condemned him, reproached him, and promised him His vengeance and punishment; and that is only because of his slander against his Lord by attributing His eternal attribute to His creation. That is where He Almighty said concerning him: 'I will cast him into Saqar' [Surah al-Muddaththir, 26]; when Allah Almighty threatened Saqar for whoever said: 'This is nothing but the word of a human' [Surah al-Muddaththir, 25], we knew that it is the word of the Creator of humans, and the word of the Creator does not resemble the word of humans; exalted is Allah above His attributes being similar and comparable. Whoever describes Allah Almighty with any meaning of human attributes has strayed and disbelieved and deserves the greatest punishment. Whoever sees this, ponders it, and knows the danger of insolence against Allah will be warned and take heed, and will refrain from such speech of the disbelievers, and will know that Allah Almighty in all His attributes is not like humans.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and proof. The author begins by affirming the creedal point that the Quran is uncreated (غير مخلوق). He immediately clarifies that this is not to be confused with the view that the sounds and letters are eternal, which he attributes to the Hanbalis out of ignorance or stubbornness. The main argument then unfolds: anyone who hears the Quran and claims it is human speech has committed slander against Allah and has disbelieved (كفر). The reason is that Allah Himself condemns such a statement in the Quran. The author cites the verses from Surah al-Muddaththir where Allah threatens with Saqar (hellfire) those who say 'This is nothing but the word of a human.' From this threat, we infer that the Quran is the word of the Creator, not of humans, and the Creator's speech is unlike human speech. The author then generalizes the principle: likening Allah's attributes to human attributes is misguidance and disbelief. He concludes with an exhortation to reflect on the seriousness of this matter and to avoid the speech of the disbelievers, ultimately affirming that Allah in all His attributes is not like humans.

Key Terms

كلام البشر
صفته القديمة
الحنابلة
سقر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that affirming the Quran is uncreated implies that the physical book or uttered sounds are eternal.
Correction: The author clarifies that the Quran as divine speech is uncreated, not the sounds and letters themselves.

Checkpoint

A) Because it denies the Quran's eloquence
B) Because Allah threatened those who say it with Saqar
C) Because it contradicts the Hanbali position

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, and anyone who claims it is human speech has committed kufr, as proven by the threat of Saqar in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran or hear it recited, do you consciously remember that you are listening to the eternal speech of Allah, or do you treat it like any other book? What would change in your heart if you truly believed that every word is from Him and unlike any human word?
?

Have you ever, even in jest or carelessness, attributed human-like qualities to Allah's attributes, such as thinking His speech resembles ours? What steps can you take to purify your belief about Allah's attributes starting today?
?
The threat of Saqar is severe. Does the fear of that punishment motivate you to honor the Quran in your daily life—by learning it, acting on it, and defending its divine status? Or have you become numb to warnings because they feel distant? What is one concrete action you will take this week to show that the Quran is, for you, the uncreated word of Allah?

The Vision of Allah is True, Without Encompassing or Modality
The author affirms the beatific vision is true and explains its nature free from modality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the vision of Allah in the afterlife is true but free from any modality or encompassing, and the proper approach to interpreting scriptural texts about divine attributes.

Core Idea
The vision of Allah is real, yet utterly unlike physical sight.

The Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the beatific vision for the believers in Paradise, but they insist it is without how, direction, or limitation. This passage from Imam al-Tahawi establishes this belief and explains why it cannot be like seeing a physical body. It also sets the methodological principle of accepting revealed texts without distorting them with personal opinions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation, noting the key statements about vision, encompassing, and modality.
Pay attention to the Quranic citation and the methodological rule.
2
Understand the affirmation
The author affirms the vision using the Quran and authentic hadith, emphasizing acceptance without reinterpretation.
3
Grasp the negation
Learn why the vision is without encompassing or modality—because Allah is not a body and not in a place or direction.
The author explains that vision depends on the nature of the seen object.
4
Reflect on the methodology
Notice the principle: we do not interpret with our opinions or desires; we submit to Allah and His Messenger and refer ambiguous matters to the All-Knowing.
This is key to the Sunni approach to divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رؤيته تعالى (حق) وَالرُّؤْيَةُ حَقٌّ لِأَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ بِغَيْرِ إِحَاطَةٍ وَلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ كَمَا نَطَقَ بِهِ كِتَابُ رَبِّنَا حَيْثُ قَالَ: وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَين نَاضِرَةُ : إِلَى رَبَّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ [سورة القيامة آية: 22، 23]، وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَلِمَهُ، وَكُلُّ مَا جَاءَ فِي ذَلِكَ مِنَ الحَدِيثِ الصَّحِيحِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَعَنْ أَصْحَابِهِ رُضْوَانُ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمَعِينَ فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ، وَمَعْنَاهُ وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَ، لَا تَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ مُتَأَوَّلِينَ بِآرَائِنَا وَلَا مُتَوَفِّمِينَ بِأَهْوَائِنَا؛ فَإِنَّهُ مَا سَلِمَ فِي دِينِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ سَلَّمَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلِرَسُولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَرَدَّ عِلْمَ مَا اشْتَبَهَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَى عَالِهِ. (و) نقول: (الرؤية) إلى الذات المقدسة المنزهة عن الإحاطة والجهة (حق)؛ أي ثابتة (الأهل الجنة)، لكن ( بغير إحاطة) بجوانب المرئي وحدوده؛ لتعاليه تعالى عن التناهي والاتصاف بالجوانب والحدود، ولا كيفية) من مقابلة وجهة وارتسام و اتصال شعاع وثبوت مسافة بين الرائي والمرئي؛ لأن هذا كله في رؤية الأجسام، والله تعالى ليس بجسم فليست رؤيته كرؤية الأجسام فإن الرؤية تابعة للشيء على ما هو عليه؛ فمن كان في مكان وجهة لا يُرى إلا في مكان وجهة كما هو كذلك ويُرى بمقابلة واتصال شعاع وثبوت مسافة، ومن لم يكن في مكان ولا جهة وليس بجسم فرؤيته كذلك ليس في مكان ولا جهة ولا بمقابلة واتصال شعاع وثبوت مسافة، وإلا لم تكن رؤية لـه بــل لغيره. كذا في شرح الطريقة لسيدي عبدالغني. قال اللقاني في شرح جوهرته والمراد أنه ينكشف سبحانه انکشافاً تاما بحاسة البصر لكل فرد من المؤمنين، وهذا مجمع عليه في الجملة وإن اختلف
His vision, exalted be He, is true. And the vision is true for the people of Paradise, without encompassing and without modality, as the Book of our Lord has spoken where He said: 'Faces that Day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' [Surah al-Qiyama, 22-23]. And its interpretation is according to what Allah Almighty intended and knows. And everything that has come in that regard from authentic hadith from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and from his Companions, may Allah be pleased with them all, it is as he said, and its meaning and interpretation are according to what He intended. We do not enter into that as those who interpret with our opinions nor as those who [؟] with our desires; for only the one who submits to Allah Almighty and His Messenger and refers the knowledge of what is ambiguous to its Knower remains safe in his religion. And we say: The vision of the sacred Essence, free from encompassing and direction, is true; that is, confirmed for the people of Paradise, but without encompassing the sides and limits of the seen object, because He is exalted above finiteness and being described with sides and limits. And without modality such as confrontation, direction, impression, connection of rays, and existence of distance between the seer and the seen, because all of this is in the vision of bodies, and Allah Almighty is not a body, so His vision is not like the vision of bodies. For vision is dependent on the thing as it is: whoever is in a place and direction can only be seen in a place and direction as such, and is seen by confrontation, connection of rays, and existence of distance; and whoever is not in a place nor direction and is not a body, his vision is likewise not in a place nor direction nor by confrontation, connection of rays, and existence of distance; otherwise it would not be a vision of him but of another. This is as mentioned in Sharh al-Tariqa of Sayyidi Abd al-Ghani. Al-Luqani said in his commentary on his Jawhara: The meaning is that He, glorified, unveils Himself completely by the sense of sight to every individual of the believers, and this is agreed upon in general, although they differed...
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the creedal belief in the vision of Allah (الرؤية) for the people of Paradise. The author first states the belief: it is true, without encompassing (إحاطة) or modality (كيفية), citing the Quranic verse 'Faces that Day will be radiant, looking at their Lord' (Surah al-Qiyama 22-23). He then explains the methodology for dealing with such texts: accept them without interpretation (تأويل) or personal desire (هوى), and refer the knowledge of ambiguous matters to Allah, who knows their true meaning. The only one safe in religion is the one who submits to Allah and His Messenger. The author then elaborates on the nature of the vision: it is a vision of the sacred Essence (الذات المقدسة), but it is free from encompassing (إحاطة) i.e., seeing sides and limits, and free from modality (كيفية) such as confrontation (مقابلة), direction (جهة), impression (ارتسام), rays (شعاع), or distance (مسافة), because these are properties of seeing physical bodies. Allah is not a body, so His vision is according to His nature—without place or direction. The author cites Sharh al-Tariqa and then al-Luqani, who says the vision is a complete unveiling (انكشاف تام) by the sense of sight for every believer, which is a point of consensus albeit with some difference in detail.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah is seen, He must be a body in a direction.
Correction: The author explains that vision is according to the nature of the seen object. Allah is not a body, so His vision is without modality or encompassing.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The vision of Allah is true for the believers in Paradise, but it is unlike physical sight and free from all modality and encompassing.
